    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_157474180" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/157474180" />
    <a title="Meredith Holley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1302775-meredith-holley"><img alt="Meredith Holley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548641865p2/1302775.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157474180?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith Holley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith Holley" href="/user/show/1302775-meredith-holley">Meredith Holley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451451385" href="/book/show/247872.The_Summer_Tree">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">grown-up Narnia fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Meredith by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4009813-kay">Kay</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157474180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16302840158440891073">Part I of this story is in many ways a grown-up <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/100915.The_Lion__the_Witch__and_the_Wardrobe__Chronicles_of_Narnia___2_' title='The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe (Chronicles of Narnia, #2) by C.S. Lewis' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lion the Witch and the Wardrobe</a>. I read the Narnia stories when I was little, and to be honest, I think C.S. Lewis will always have a place in my heart. To me, he’s a sort of philosophical grandpa, whom I ignore when he’s spouting cultural faux pas, but who brings out something lovely and profound at least as often as he says something unfortunate. Anyway, this book is not about C.S. Lewis, but I think the affection I feel for Narnia made a dif</span>
  <span id="freeText16302840158440891073" style="display:none">Part I of this story is in many ways a grown-up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/100915.The_Lion__the_Witch__and_the_Wardrobe__Chronicles_of_Narnia___2_" title="The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe (Chronicles of Narnia, #2) by C.S. Lewis" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lion the Witch and the Wardrobe</a>. I read the Narnia stories when I was little, and to be honest, I think C.S. Lewis will always have a place in my heart. To me, he’s a sort of philosophical grandpa, whom I ignore when he’s spouting cultural faux pas, but who brings out something lovely and profound at least as often as he says something unfortunate. Anyway, this book is not about C.S. Lewis, but I think the affection I feel for Narnia made a difference in my read of this book. I also don’t think I need Lewis to be 100% correct all the time, and that probably made a difference in me liking the way Kay made the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Christ <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> story his own. <br /><br />I spend a lot of time complaining, I think, about when authors throw together a really bad recipe for a book – when they mutilate and mix ingredients that should never go together. I really liked the use of the ingredients here. There’s Narnia; Henry IV / rakishness; some wild-west, bow-and-arrow stuff; a very decent hair-color change; law and folklore; a magical mystery animal; and a giant black swan that smells like garbage. Basically pretty good. I’m not a lover of fantasy (sorry!), so I have to get past the orcs and dwarves and elves to like a story like this (and I don’t care if you call them different names, they’re still orcs and elves). I’ll probably talk more about that in my review of the second book in this series, but with this book it’s pretty easy to look past to some genuinely good stories.<br /><br />Unfortunately, at this point, probably most of what I have to say is a spoiler. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I thought the use of the Christ story was really lovely. I particularly liked the disagreement as to whether the sacrifice on the Summer Tree was for good or evil. I am a little disappointed that the questioning of the good of the Summer Tree ended up being wrong (maybe this will turn around in the next couple of books, I don’t know), and that the argument never really gets addressed again after Paul comes back from the dead. I think it’s more interesting and tragic if it had turned out to be a clear mistake. I do appreciate, though, that the leader of the CBS Orchestra for the Late Show with David Letterman is the Christ figure in this. I mean, who else would you choose when you’re Canadian? (this book is Canadian, fyi, but you probably know that if you clicked the spoiler button.) Here’s the thing that bothers me about it: you’ve got this guy who feels a lot of guilt, (like, torturous guilt) so he volunteers to commit suicide to save the universe, and it’s a really good idea. I don’t like that, to be totally honest. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Okay, maybe fewer spoilers than I thought. The other problem I have with this is the characterization of the gods. Maybe this is just a personal pet peeve, but a lot of times I don’t like the characterization of deities in gender roles (the obvious exception to this is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1371.The_Iliad" title="The Iliad by Homer" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iliad</a>, which, of course, rules); I prefer the Julian of Norwich god who is both male and female because I'm less likely to see the female god relegated to the kitchen. There’s some other gender stuff that goes on in these books that makes me a little put off. I don’t think it’s insidious, or anything, I just think it takes away from the entertainment. Like, the priestesses are dangerous and suspicious, but the magicians are noble and trustworthy. But, then when everything gets sexy, the girls aren’t scary anymore. I’m not saying it stays like that the whole time, but, I don’t know. It just has a little bit of a male-culture feel that isn’t super entertaining to me. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Like, also, when they’re all out hunting in the fields and glorying in their manhood and then the kid gets the best spirit-animal EVER and it’s a unicorn/Pegasus? What is up with that? Like, dude, She-Ra did it better. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Anyway, I feel like I’m kind of ragging on this book, when I really did like it. I really like the Henry IV storyline, and I like the Seer stuff. I like that they’re all a bunch of Canadian kids and that there’s a law student who really needs to study for Evidence. I like how it assumes the vital importance to the WHOLE UNIVERSE of Celtic folklore. That’s pretty cool. I think Jennifer’s story isn’t really fair, and even though I’m almost through the second book, I still don’t really get it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So, the Satan character targeted Jennifer because destroying her is really important to destroying the universe? Or, just because she’s pretty and he doesn’t have a grander concept for it? If he's willing to waste his time like that, he doesn't seem so intimidating to me. Also, there’s something about her getting tortured that seemed really blunt. I don’t know how to explain my confusion better than that. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But, in general, I think the story used some really great legends really creatively. I liked it. I think I should have felt more emotionally attached to the characters, but I think that has more to do with how I feel in general right now than the book itself. Especially if you like fantasy, and especially if you're willing to commit to thousands of pages of fantasy reading (because there is a mammoth cliffhanger at the end of this book), it is worth picking up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16302840158440891073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <u>The Review</u>
</b><br/><br/>I generally don't write a review for a book unless I finish it. I don't think it's fair to the author or to others interested in the book. <br/><br/>I didn't finish this book. <br/><br/>However, I did spend a significant amount of time on this book, so I think I do have the right to say something.<br/><br/>Wow.   <span id="freeText13118146443693903487" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>The Review</u>
</b><br /><br />I generally don't write a review for a book unless I finish it. I don't think it's fair to the author or to others interested in the book. <br /><br />I didn't finish this book. <br /><br />However, I did spend a significant amount of time on this book, so I think I do have the right to say something.<br /><br />Wow. This book beat me. I don't know if was the method in which I read the book or if I just didn't have the mindset to do so, but I just didn't like it. <br /><br />Reading became a chore and something that I didn't look forward to. I found myself halfway through and seeing the light at the end of the tunnel. <br /><br />Then I thought, reading a book of this type shouldn't be a chore. I shouldn't be looking forward to ending the story, but savoring what's happening in the narrative currently.<br /><br />So I quit. If you can get through it, congratulations. Reading should be a pleasure and not a labor for which Hercules would pat you on the back in admiration.<br /><br />I don't think it's objectively a bad book. I'm sure it possesses a certain charm and that maybe the series turns into a compelling read in the later books. It was just lost or wasted on me, I guess.<br /><br />This series probably has its fans, and I'm sure they would disagree with my assessment. I'm not saying that they are wrong. I'm saying that I just didn't get it or like it.<br /><br /></span>

    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588746288p2/10326608.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11399860438200898522">This review is from my reread of this series in 2015/16.<br/><br/>The Fionavar Tapestry was a formative work for me in many ways, with my first read from soon after they came out in the 80s and with multiple rereads since. I mention this to explain why I'm not completely objective on them, as there are several issues from the lens of a 21st century reader including the way some of the women are portrayed here and the lack diversity in a book set across multiple countries and peoples that is meant to be th</span>
  <span id="freeText11399860438200898522" style="display:none">This review is from my reread of this series in 2015/16.<br /><br />The Fionavar Tapestry was a formative work for me in many ways, with my first read from soon after they came out in the 80s and with multiple rereads since. I mention this to explain why I'm not completely objective on them, as there are several issues from the lens of a 21st century reader including the way some of the women are portrayed here and the lack diversity in a book set across multiple countries and peoples that is meant to be the "first world" that all our worlds are a reflection of (maybe a very small slice of Western Europe, not so much anywhere else).<br /><br />Five Canadian university students travel to a secondary fantasy world, Fionavar supposedly to celebrate the 50th anniversary of the reign of Ailell dan Art, High King of Brennin. Each finds an important role to play in the events of the series. It's at this time that the evil god Rakoth Maugrim breaks free from his prison and declares war on the whole world.<br /><br />Volumes have been written on this series, regarding the use of mythology in fantasy works and the price of power and sacrifice. It's all worthwhile, but tends to detract from the shear emotional impact of the series as it constantly defines what is mythic and legendary and then exceeds the legends by the actions of people and gods of the current day. There's a palpable sense of greatness in the sacrifices and actions of these people, particularly in this volume with the actions of Paul, Kim and Ysane and even the Prince Diarmuid who initially comes across as rude and unlikable but soon demonstrates hidden depths.<br /><br />This is only my current reread, I very much doubt it will be my last.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11399860438200898522" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3598362868" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3598362868" />
    <a title="Sebastien Castell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4846758-sebastien-castell"><img alt="Sebastien Castell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378071485p2/4846758.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3598362868?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sebastien Castell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sebastien Castell" href="/user/show/4846758-sebastien-castell">Sebastien Castell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4846758-sebastien-castell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3598362868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17175468780452566602">I wonder if everyone has their favourite era of fantasy, and whether that era corresponds to when they first truly became enthralled with the genre. For me, it was mid-1980's. It's not that fantasy was better in those days; in fact, I'll bet any number of literary scholars would argue earlier works were more innovative and more recent ones more sophisticated and inclusive. But the language and style of the 1980's were the ones that I first learned and that stuck with me. It's easier, somehow, to</span>
  <span id="freeText17175468780452566602" style="display:none">I wonder if everyone has their favourite era of fantasy, and whether that era corresponds to when they first truly became enthralled with the genre. For me, it was mid-1980's. It's not that fantasy was better in those days; in fact, I'll bet any number of literary scholars would argue earlier works were more innovative and more recent ones more sophisticated and inclusive. But the language and style of the 1980's were the ones that I first learned and that stuck with me. It's easier, somehow, to read a fantasy novel written in that era – as if I'm not fighting the language quite so much.<br />But there were other things I liked about 1980's fantasy. Urban fantasy was driven by a kind of blending of ancient and modern mythologies and hadn't yet been taken over by paranormal romance and poorly-disguised superhero stories minus the capes and tights. Portal fantasy novels asked how adults from our world might react when dropped into a magical and mythical landscape. Nowadays, portal fantasy is largely relegated to middle-grade books and variations on LitRPG (literary role playing games), both of which are fine in their own right, but not really for me.<br />All of which brings me to The Summer Tree by Guy Gavriel Kay.<br />I first read found this book in the discard trolley of my local library, bought in for a quarter, and fell headlong and forever into Fionavar, a land not dissimilar in many ways to Middle Earth (Kay had recently come off helping Christopher Tolkien with The Silmarillion) but without hobbits. In their place come five twenty-somethings from our world, struggling to figure out how to survive amidst all the swordplay, magic, and evil forces, yet also discovering that they, too, have a vital place in this world.<br />So far it probably doesn't sound all that inventive, partly because most of us have come across lots of portal fantasies over the years and partly because I haven't conveyed what made the Summer Tree so special: the feeling and the voice.<br />Typically when you drop someone from our world into a fantasy world, you can expect about three hundred pages of, "Oh my god, this is nuts! WTF! Like, I totally don't buy this 'Dark Lord' stuff at all, but geez, there's that guy with a sword coming for me just like in [insert intertextual reference about recent movie or video game]". It's not an unexpected thing for writers to do, but it's a facile way of simulating realism and internal conflict.<br />Guy Gavriel Kay, however, goes the opposite route. In the Summer Tree, the "I don't believe this stuff" comes and goes quickly, which feels more realistic to me because it's hard to imagine still telling yourself something's a dream when you've nearly had your head chopped off. Instead, his characters find in themselves these nagging resonances with the world of Fionavar, and often slip into the more lyrical language style of the peoples of that world. It changes them from lost mall shoppers in Mordor to semi-mythic beings themselves.<br />Part of how Kay accomplishes this (or at least, what it looks like to me as a reader) is by giving those characters genuine heartaches and insecurities that they're carrying with them into Fionavar. So instead of whining about their latest breakups, the five have real, enduring wounds that they're wrestling to heal, and in those wounds lies their particular roles inside the unfolding epic battle for Fionavar.<br />Re-reading this book more than thirty years after it was written, I was struck by how fresh it feels to me simply because it's got a genuinely different style than most other fantasy novels I pick up. It's not a style that will suit everyone (and getting used to a head-hopping omniscient narration can be jarring), but personally? I loved it.<br />Good and bad things happen to characters in this story, and with each one, they're transformed. They don't go back to old insecurities but instead move forward, becoming, step by step, the heroes Fionavar needs. The characters native to Fionavar are equally fleshed-out, and the mythic characters brought into the story (there's a whole Arthurian thing that comes into play) are blissfully changed by events rather than being stock repetitions of iconic figures.<br />The Summer Tree is the first in a trilogy, and unlike modern fantasy each book isn't phone-book sized. This keeps the pacing fast and the storytelling fluid. I doubt Kay would argue that this was his best book (given, I think, that it was his first), but it's got a romantic compulsion about heroism that I adored even all these years later.<br />Not everyone will react as positively to the Summer Tree as me – this is very much a book of its time that doesn't explicitly or implicitly make reference to the intertextual "meta-ness" that so characterizes contemporary fantasy. But for me, as someone who discovered fantasy in the 1980's, The Summer Tree will always remain one of my favourites.<br />Now, onto book two: The Wandering Fire.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17175468780452566602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_18618552" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18618552" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18618552?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451451385" href="/book/show/247872.The_Summer_Tree">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=canadian-lit">canadian-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=shabby">shabby</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=drunken-reviews">drunken-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=sword-and-sorcery-opera">sword-and-sorcery-opera</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18618552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer67833721229816167">I am so glad I came to Kay's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1148721.The_Fionavar_Tapestry' title='The Fionavar Tapestry by Guy Gavriel Kay' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Fionavar Tapestry</a> late because I doubt I ever would have read his great books if I had read these first. <br/><br/>I was acting in a play with my great friend Jefferson when he suggested I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104085.A_Song_for_Arbonne' title='A Song for Arbonne by Guy Gavriel Kay' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Song For Arbonne</a>. I was blown away. He told me to read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104089.Tigana' title='Tigana by Guy Gavriel Kay' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tigana</a>. I loved Brandon and was in love with Kay. He told me to read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104101.The_Lions_of_al_Rassan' title='The Lions of al-Rassan by Guy Gavriel Kay' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lions of Al-Rassan</a>, which I've read numerous times since, and I had found my favourite Kay. He told me to avoid the trilogy, though, because he knew I wo</span>
  <span id="freeText67833721229816167" style="display:none">I am so glad I came to Kay's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1148721.The_Fionavar_Tapestry" title="The Fionavar Tapestry by Guy Gavriel Kay" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fionavar Tapestry</a> late because I doubt I ever would have read his great books if I had read these first. <br /><br />I was acting in a play with my great friend Jefferson when he suggested I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104085.A_Song_for_Arbonne" title="A Song for Arbonne by Guy Gavriel Kay" rel="nofollow noopener">A Song For Arbonne</a>. I was blown away. He told me to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104089.Tigana" title="Tigana by Guy Gavriel Kay" rel="nofollow noopener">Tigana</a>. I loved Brandon and was in love with Kay. He told me to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104101.The_Lions_of_al_Rassan" title="The Lions of al-Rassan by Guy Gavriel Kay" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lions of Al-Rassan</a>, which I've read numerous times since, and I had found my favourite Kay. He told me to avoid the trilogy, though, because he knew I would hate it. I don't hate it, but it is the worst writing of Kay's career. <br /><br />Overdetermined. One of my favourite words. And this trilogy, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/104086.The_Summer_Tree__The_Fionavar_Tapestry___1_" title="The Summer Tree (The Fionavar Tapestry, #1) by Guy Gavriel Kay" rel="nofollow noopener">The Summer Tree</a>, is that. Paul is crucified on the Summer Tree and the number three plays an important role. How sneakily Christian of you Guy. Dave goes native. How sneakily Anglo-Native American of you Guy. Kimberly becomes a seer. How Earth Mother of you Guy. Bla, bla, bla.<br /><br />Loren Silvercloak (Gandalf anyone?) and his bitch, Matt Sören,the obligatory little person, are there. We have our heroes, we have our villains, our shabby rulers, our lands in crisis, our crappy Fantasy tropes galore. And who cares?<br /><br />I wanted to care. But I didn't. I couldn't. I'd already read Kay's good stuff -- maybe even his great stuff -- and going back to his freshman work was depressing. I wanted to love it. But I could barely like it. <br /><br />Bummer. </span>
  <a data-text-id="67833721229816167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_175212039" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/175212039" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1256603-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596206765p2/1256603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/175212039?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1256603-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/33667571-the-summer-tree">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256603-sara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256603-sara?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer175212039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer702120819490252603">This is one of those five star books that I've always been reluctant to actually review. Partly because Guy Gavriel Kay is a writer of such a high caliber that writing about his writing feels more than a little ridiculous. Like anything I have to say is going to sound like "duhhh dis wuz real good!" next to the actual book. But also partly because Kay's writing has always sort of defied description. He writes epic fantasy of the highest order but getting into how affecting his writing is, how it</span>
  <span id="freeText702120819490252603" style="display:none">This is one of those five star books that I've always been reluctant to actually review. Partly because Guy Gavriel Kay is a writer of such a high caliber that writing about his writing feels more than a little ridiculous. Like anything I have to say is going to sound like "duhhh dis wuz real good!" next to the actual book. But also partly because Kay's writing has always sort of defied description. He writes epic fantasy of the highest order but getting into how affecting his writing is, how its often brought me to tears, that's harder to get down somehow.<br /><br />The Fionavar Tapestry is Kay's magnum opus, his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5091.The_Dark_Tower__The_Dark_Tower___7_" title="The Dark Tower (The Dark Tower, #7) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dark Tower</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___1_3_" title="The Lord of the Rings (The Lord of the Rings, #1-3) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lord of the Rings</a>. Which is interesting because the premise of the series is predicated on the idea that the land of Fionavar is the source of every other fantasy world ever created, it is the heart from which all the others are born. There's a gravity to it, a holiness and a reverence that makes you want to talk about its legends and history in a hushed voice. You are speaking of something sacred when you speak of Fionavar.<br /><br />The basic story is a simple one that many other fantasy novels and series have used. A group of college friends are taken by magic to Fionavar and tasked with helping quell the darkness that threatens to destroy it and thus all other worlds. Kevin, Paul, Dave, Kimberly, and Jennifer all have their roles to play in the coming wars and they each have their private struggles with fear and anger and regret before they can realize their destinies.<br /><br />This is probably the most elegant series I've ever read and has always sort of defined "high" fantasy for me. The language helps. Kay is a poet and is able to have his characters, modern day 20 somethings, proclaim their love for each other in the style of epic poets or make huge declarations of war and it never feels cheesy or remotely out of place and I've never, ever encountered another author who could pull that off. They think beautifully, their inner monologues all have a depth of feeling that should be melodramatic but somehow isn't. Its like those rare moments in really great musical theater where the actors sing because they have no other choice. I can't imagine Kay's characters speaking in any other way. <br /><br />There's a solemnity to this series that I just adore. And everything is built on a foundation of love, a theme that runs through virtually all of Kay's writing. Even the epic battle being fought between the forces of good and evil is founded on a broken heart.<br /><br />This is a series to be savored. Take it from an expert in the art of skipping through to the end when the going gets tough. You will want to read every word. I haven't even touched the epic quests, star crossed love, or magical battles. If I got into the elves and the dwarves and gods we'd be here for a year.<br /><br />But Fionavar is best discovered on your own the way I did. That's how most magical journey's start anyway isn't it? With a wrong turn or a chance encounter or the moment when your hand touches the spine of a beautifully bound book and you take it home without even reading the title because you just have a feeling about this one.<br /><br />1/8/2019 Just a quick addendum having now listened to this one through Audible. The only thing that could have made the experience of reading these books better was a really terrific narration. This was indeed delivered in spades by Simon Vance (who also does a very fine Jonathan Harker in Audible's "Dracula" which I will one day finish) who reads the story like some kind of legendary bard out of a fantasy epic. Which is of course entirely appropriate. He's got a sonorous, rich voice that floats effortlessly between stalwart kings, world crushing demons, and cold high priestesses. His voice seems as thought it was made to speak Kay's words. </span>
  <a data-text-id="702120819490252603" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12618093578759714179">5.0 stars. I just finished re-reading this book and was blown away by it. This is intelligent High Fantasy at its best. Gay Gavriel Kay is an incredible writer and his world building as fantastic. It is hard to be original in this well-worn genre, but Kay pulls it off and makes his characters and the world-setting unique and fresh. <br/><br/>Highly recommended!!!</span>

<div id="review_266549292" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/266549292" />
    <a title="Nicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/223837-nicky"><img alt="Nicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/266549292?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=based-on-myth-saga-etc">based-on-myth-saga-etc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer266549292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16990482724654957939">Fresh from reading most of Tolkien's work, and writing a gigantic essay on it too, I have a different perspective on Kay's work. Especially when reminded that Kay worked on The Silmarillion with Christopher Tolkien. He has a lot in common with Tolkien, really: the synthesis of a new mythology (though not done as history, and therefore lacking all the little authenticating details that Tolkien put in) using elements of an old one (though Kay used Celtic and Norse mythology, and goodness knows wha</span>
  <span id="freeText16990482724654957939" style="display:none">Fresh from reading most of Tolkien's work, and writing a gigantic essay on it too, I have a different perspective on Kay's work. Especially when reminded that Kay worked on The Silmarillion with Christopher Tolkien. He has a lot in common with Tolkien, really: the synthesis of a new mythology (though not done as history, and therefore lacking all the little authenticating details that Tolkien put in) using elements of an old one (though Kay used Celtic and Norse mythology, and goodness knows what else). The comparisons can't help but be made, though Kay sees his world as a tapestry and Tolkien as a song being sung.<br /><br />I don't think he makes his world as well as Tolkien does. I feel info-dumped, at times, rather than as if I'm just touching on the tip of a giant submerged mass of lore and wonder that even the inhabitants of his world only half-know. His gods are much more touchable, and more concerned with the individual fates of mortal men, and so less distant and thus less awe-inspiring. I think, perhaps more like C.S. Lewis, he tries to handle more than he can really weave together.<br /><br />But, that's not to say it's totally unsuccessful. A book that can have me laughing at one moment and weeping not three pages later can't exactly be classed as unsuccessful. His style is distancing at first -- perhaps too much of a high tone, which Tolkien avoided with his hobbits -- but there are some lovely lines and turns of phrase, and undoubtedly he makes me care about the characters.<br /><br />Another hint that he's doing quite well is that this is at least my fourth reread of this trilogy, though I could well have read it more than that.<br /><br />Not perfect, but beloved all the same.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16990482724654957939" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_120358542" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120358542" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120358542?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/9249194-the-summer-tree">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120358542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1523671836564529948">I'm going to start my review of this book with some, at least slightly negative comments, so...before I do so let me say that I liked the book pretty well and am giving it 4 stars (I'd probably go 3.5+ if I had that option, but I don't).<br/><br/>I tried to read this book (these books as it's a trilogy) some years ago and was, shall we say, far from enamored with them. I put The Summer Tree down as not worth my time and didn't go back to it. Recently I've seen some reviews by people whom I've agreed with </span>
  <span id="freeText1523671836564529948" style="display:none">I'm going to start my review of this book with some, at least slightly negative comments, so...before I do so let me say that I liked the book pretty well and am giving it 4 stars (I'd probably go 3.5+ if I had that option, but I don't).<br /><br />I tried to read this book (these books as it's a trilogy) some years ago and was, shall we say, far from enamored with them. I put The Summer Tree down as not worth my time and didn't go back to it. Recently I've seen some reviews by people whom I've agreed with on other books that were "very" positive so, I decided to give it another go. I was down with a bad cold recently and on nothing but audio books (headache) so I reserved this one on audio... <br /><br />Now, first the sulfur, then later you can have the molasses to help it go down. The book hits a few of my "oh my goodness this again" spots. For one thing, there was a time that I'd just been "King Arthured" to death. It seemed for a while that for every 3 books on the fantasy shelves...two of them would be a "wonderful re-imagining of the Arthurian Legend" we had books from Arthur's point of view, Guenevere's point of view, Mordred's point of view, Lancelot's point of view, Morgan Le Fay's point of view...and possibly Author's horse's point of view. I was burned out, and am not much better now. Show me a blurb that says a book is "an exciting new ,take on, version of, or re-imagining of the Arthurian legend" and I'll show you a book that's going back on the shelf. <br /><br />We also have the constantly annoying "battle of the sexes" motif built into the book. Wheel of time anyone? The only saving grace is it's not quite as annoying here as it was/and still is there.<br /><br />The book is liberally leavened with ideas, stereotypes, and archetypes that you will undoubtedly recognize.<br /><br />Now, all that being said, the book is pretty well written and I have no doubt that should GGK run across this review or one like it, he'd say something like "ya...well show me your best seller!" He'd be right of course. Given a chance the book's story "can" draw you in. You need to let it however. I am now starting The Wandering Fire and I don't know how I'll like it, but I'll give it a chance. My final take...not a bad read. Don't love it, but I do like it, a little. 4 stars...because 3.5 isn't possible. :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="1523671836564529948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_474617092" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/474617092" />
    <a title="Wanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda"><img alt="Wanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528903039p2/9246169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/474617092?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wanda" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda">Wanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=reading-project">reading-project</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=when-words-collide">when-words-collide</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=canadian-eh">canadian-eh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer474617092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14406532249897966767">This is Guy Gavriel Kay’s earliest published novel. I’m sure there were previous books that didn’t get published, because you don’t become such a skilled writer without plenty of practice. To be fair, I have previously read two of his more recent novels (set in Ancient China) which are masterful and The Summer Tree is very obviously an early entry in his oeuvre. It is very complex, there are many characters, and there is a LOT going on. A very ambitious novel.<br/><br/>Okay, up front I have to say that I </span>
  <span id="freeText14406532249897966767" style="display:none">This is Guy Gavriel Kay’s earliest published novel. I’m sure there were previous books that didn’t get published, because you don’t become such a skilled writer without plenty of practice. To be fair, I have previously read two of his more recent novels (set in Ancient China) which are masterful and The Summer Tree is very obviously an early entry in his oeuvre. It is very complex, there are many characters, and there is a LOT going on. A very ambitious novel.<br /><br />Okay, up front I have to say that I adore the King Arthur story cycle and I have a true love for Norse and British mythology. Plus, I have a serious love affair with Tolkien’s <i>Lord of the Rings</i>. These predilections predispose me to love this novel and this series. It makes complete sense to me that Kay, who worked with Christopher Tolkien to get <i>The Silmarillion</i> edited to publish, would be heavily influenced by Tolkien’s world. <br /><br />What I appreciate is his spin on things Tolkien. Yes, there are dwarves who delve in the earth and there are elf-equivalents (lios alfar) but they behave in GGK ways, not just Tolkien ways. He also takes a page from Donaldson (the Thomas Covenant series) in having modern people transported into an alternate world, but in my opinion he does it so much better (by orders of magnitude). Plus, instead of just being a completely different world with different rules, Fionavar is related to our world. Fionavar is the master copy and our world is one of many versions of it.<br /><br />Also a plus for me was prominent female characters with substantial roles to play in the action, although <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was disappointed that all he could think of to torment Jennifer was overwhelming sexual assault. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I hadn’t meant to read the second book until sometime in January, but somehow I just grabbed <i>The Wandering Fire</i> and plunged back into the story immediately. I expect I will be too involved to pause between it and <i>The Darkest Road</i> either. One of the benefits of reading an older series is not having to wait for the next installment. A complete joy to read.<br /><br />Possibly, because I know it is not on par with Kay’s more recent works, I should give it a 4 star rating, but I enjoyed it so much that it’s getting 5 stars. With only 5 stars and no half stars, we are working with a fairly blunt instrument when it comes to ratings.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14406532249897966767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_339292947" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/339292947" />
    <a title="Dawn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2517340-dawn"><img alt="Dawn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480301169p2/2517340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/339292947?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawn" href="/user/show/2517340-dawn">Dawn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2517340-dawn?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2517340-dawn?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer339292947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15593696404505218407">This book has been on my to-read list for a long time. I've read other Kay (and loved it all), but for some reason I just kept putting this one off. Every time I decided it was time to jump in, I'd read the blurb and decide to go with something else. "<i>Five men and women find themselves flung into the magical land of Fionavar, First of all Worlds.</i>" Yeah.. About that.. The whole magically transported into a fantasy world thing? Thanks but no thanks. It just doesn't do it for me.<br/><br/>So needless to say,</span>
  <span id="freeText15593696404505218407" style="display:none">This book has been on my to-read list for a long time. I've read other Kay (and loved it all), but for some reason I just kept putting this one off. Every time I decided it was time to jump in, I'd read the blurb and decide to go with something else. "<i>Five men and women find themselves flung into the magical land of Fionavar, First of all Worlds.</i>" Yeah.. About that.. The whole magically transported into a fantasy world thing? Thanks but no thanks. It just doesn't do it for me.<br /><br />So needless to say, I went into this sort of dreading it and not really expecting to like it. And for about the first 25 - 30% of the story, it lived up to that expectation. One of my biggest gripes with the transported into a fantasy world thing is how unbelievable trusting people are. "Hey! I can do magic! We're going to take you to a magical world to meet our King! Are you in?" And of course... They're in. And when it actually happens, when they actually pop into existence in another world, complete acceptance. I don't know about you, but if it were me... First, I'd think whoever was asking me to go was on drugs, and I would call the police so they could come pick up the crazy man wearing a robe... Then, if I still managed to somehow make it to the other world, I'd kick the crazy man's ass thinking that they somehow managed to drug me.<br /><br />So like I said.. Auto-strike against it. Another problem I had with the first 30%, there are a lot of main characters. The POV bounces around a lot, and with so many characters, you don't have much time to connect to any of them. I spent a lot of time forgetting who was who, and then figuring it out and not really caring.. It was not a good time.<br /><br />But then somewhere around chapter seven (about 40%), it all clicked. And after that... Wow. It was beautiful. I was moved over and over again by the story, the writing, the characters... Everything. It was so strange... I was pretty much committed to not really liking this one, and then all of a sudden I feel myself tearing up, my heart pounding, completely wrapped up in the words I was reading. I went from forcing myself to pick it up and read a little, to hating the fact that my lunch break was over and I had to put it down. Suddenly the characters who I had spend the first 30% feeling disconnected from came alive to me. And when the characters came alive.. So did the world.<br /><br />So against all odds, I ended up really loving this book. I can't wait to read the rest of the trilogy, this is how good traditional fantasy is done. I'm only giving it 4 stars instead of 5, because of the rocky start, but depending on how the rest of the story plays out.. I have a feeling this will be jumping onto my favorites shelf very soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15593696404505218407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_832420103" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/832420103" />
    <a title="Robyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25037254-robyn"><img alt="Robyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532341155p2/25037254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/832420103?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robyn" href="/user/show/25037254-robyn">Robyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25037254-robyn?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer832420103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8979325789867473326">This is the kind of high fantasy that I can easily see re-reading, and rather wish I had come to earlier in life. (It's definitely not a kid's book, but I'd almost rather my fictional progeny read this than Narnia.) Kay takes touchstones from mythology and weaves them together in a haunting opener to this trilogy about the first world and the impact five people from our own world have on it, in the midst of an epic struggle between good and evil. <br/><br/>It's not without it's issues, but they're easily </span>
  <span id="freeText8979325789867473326" style="display:none">This is the kind of high fantasy that I can easily see re-reading, and rather wish I had come to earlier in life. (It's definitely not a kid's book, but I'd almost rather my fictional progeny read this than Narnia.) Kay takes touchstones from mythology and weaves them together in a haunting opener to this trilogy about the first world and the impact five people from our own world have on it, in the midst of an epic struggle between good and evil. <br /><br />It's not without it's issues, but they're easily overlooked in favour of just how darn enticing this story is. I can't wait to read the next ones. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8979325789867473326" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1086949222" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1086949222" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23841736-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532221628p2/23841736.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1086949222?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/23841736-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23841736-sarah?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23841736-sarah?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy-challenge-2015">sci-fi-fantasy-challenge-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1086949222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1806386996208974448">I really enjoyed this story. I did have a few quibbles, mainly that the way that the story had people from our world transported into this fantasy world was quite jarring. I can see where this is his first novel but it's a novel of an author finding his sea legs and I'm looking forward to how the rest of the series develops.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MftqKXFad8yqeRi/XuFuEjZJvvTm4MfT4EyzNSBPQE8VQh7FRjCikYhUTYTgSuaYGnVy6tuL6sknVXObM6tf+w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vg6WeTeEbnE0ii1JAlWwzp6zMFycHIbDc/nfZ/UbzOqat+KVAO67LBaneHK8/jhEso/8QqF3q9m04B/J5v/TXg==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/60177.Guy_Gavriel_Kay">About Guy Gavriel Kay</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/60177.Guy_Gavriel_Kay"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1218804723p3/60177.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>

<a href="/author/show/60177.Guy_Gavriel_Kay">Guy Gavriel Kay
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
6,131
followers

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1428017278929884370">Guy Gavriel Kay is a Canadian author of fantasy fiction. Many of his novels are set in fictional realms that resemble real places during real historical periods, such as Constantinople during the reign of Justinian I or Spain during the time of El Cid. Those works are published and marketed as historical fantasy, though the author himself has expressed a preference to shy away from genre categoriz</span>
  <span id="freeText1428017278929884370" style="display:none">Guy Gavriel Kay is a Canadian author of fantasy fiction. Many of his novels are set in fictional realms that resemble real places during real historical periods, such as Constantinople during the reign of Justinian I or Spain during the time of El Cid. Those works are published and marketed as historical fantasy, though the author himself has expressed a preference to shy away from genre categorization when possible.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1428017278929884370" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
